They will always all be blissfully\n// unaware of each other's existence, even when their messages are being multiplexed together by\n// ADS.\n//\n// There are two scenarios which affect how DeltaSubscriptionState manages the resources. First\n// scenario is when we are subscribed to a wildcard resource, and other scenario is when we are not.\n//\n// Delta subscription state also divides the resources it cached into three categories: requested,\n// wildcard and ambiguous.\n//\n// The \"requested\" category is for resources that we have explicitly asked for (either through the\n// initial set of resources or through the on-demand mechanism). Resources in this category are in\n// one of two states: \"complete\" and \"waiting for server\".\n//\n// \"Complete\" resources are resources about which the server sent us the information we need (for\n// now - just resource version).\n//\n// The \"waiting for server\" state is either for resources that we have just requested, but we still\n// didn't receive any version information from the server, or for the \"complete\" resources that,\n// according to the server, are gone, but we are still interested in them - in such case we strip\n// the information from the resource.\n//\n// The \"wildcard\" category is for resources that we are not explicitly interested in, but we are\n// indirectly interested through the subscription to the wildcard resource.\n//\n// The \"ambiguous\" category is for resources that we stopped being interested in, but we may still\n// be interested indirectly through the wildcard subscription. This situation happens because of the\n// xDS protocol limitation - the server isn't able to tell us that the resource we subscribed to is\n// also a part of our wildcard subscription. So when we unsubscribe from the resource, we need to\n// receive a confirmation from the server whether to keep the resource (which means that it was a\n// part of our wildcard subscription) or to drop it.\n//\n// Please refer to drawings (non-wildcard-resource-state-machine.png and\n// (wildcard-resource-state-machine.png) for visual depictions of the resource state machine.\n//\n// In the \"no wildcard subscription\" scenario all the cached resources should be in the \"requested\"\n// category. Resources are added to the category upon the explicit request and dropped when we\n// explicitly unsubscribe from it. Transitions between \"complete\" and \"waiting for server\" happen\n// when we receive messages from the server - if a resource in the message is in \"added resources\"\n// list (thus contains version information), the resource becomes \"complete\". If the resource in the\n// message is in \"removed resources\" list, it changes into the \"waiting for server\" state. If a\n// server sends us a resource that we didn't request, it's going to be ignored.\n//\n// In the \"wildcard subscription\" scenario, \"requested\" category is the same as in \"no wildcard\n// subscription\" scenario, with one exception - the unsubscribed \"complete\" resource is not removed\n// from the cache, but it's moved to the \"ambiguous\" resources instead. At this point we are waiting\n// for the server to tell us that this resource should be either moved to the \"wildcard\" resources,\n// or dropped. Resources in \"wildcard\" category are only added there or dropped from there by the\n// server. Resources from both \"wildcard\" and \"ambiguous\" categories can become \"requested\"\n// \"complete\" resources if we subscribe to them again.\n//\n// The delta subscription state transitions between the two scenarios depending on whether we are\n// subscribed to wildcard resource or not. Nothing special happens when we transition from \"no\n// wildcard subscription\" to \"wildcard subscription\" scenario, but when transitioning in the other\n// direction, we drop all the resources in \"wildcard\" and \"ambiguous\" categories.\nclass DeltaSubscriptionState : public Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::config> {\npublic:\n  DeltaSubscriptionState(std::string type_url, UntypedConfigUpdateCallbacks& watch_map,\n                         const LocalInfo::LocalInfo& local_info, Event::Dispatcher& dispatcher,\n                         XdsConfigTrackerOptRef xds_config_tracker);\n\n  // Update which resources we're interested in subscribing to.\n  void updateSubscriptionInterest(const absl::flat_hash_set<std::string>& cur_added,\n                                  const absl::flat_hash_set<std::string>& cur_removed);\n  void setMustSendDiscoveryRequest() { must_send_discovery_request_ = true; }\n\n  // Whether there was a change in our subscription interest we have yet to inform the server of.\n  bool subscriptionUpdatePending() const;\n\n  void markStreamFresh() { any_request_sent_yet_in_current_stream_ = false; }\n\n  UpdateAck handleResponse(const envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryResponse& message);\n\n  void handleEstablishmentFailure();\n\n  // Returns the next gRPC request proto to be sent off to the server, based on this object's\n  // understanding of the current protocol state, and new resources that Envoy wants to request.\n  envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryRequest getNextRequestAckless();","numLines":100,"startLine":1,"totalLines":183}}}

Reestablishes the gRPC channel when necessary, and provides rate limiting of\n// requests.\ntemplate <class RequestProto, class ResponseProto>\nclass GrpcStream : public GrpcStreamInterface<RequestProto, ResponseProto>,\n                   public Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::config> {\npublic:\n  GrpcStream(GrpcStreamCallbacks<ResponseProto>* callbacks, Grpc::RawAsyncClientPtr async_client,\n             const Protobuf::MethodDescriptor& service_method, Event::Dispatcher& dispatcher,\n             Stats::Scope& scope, BackOffStrategyPtr backoff_strategy,\n             const RateLimitSettings& rate_limit_settings)\n      : callbacks_(callbacks), async_client_(std::move(async_client)),\n        service_method_(service_method),\n        control_plane_stats_(Utility::generateControlPlaneStats(scope)),\n        time_source_(dispatcher.timeSource()), backoff_strategy_(std::move(backoff_strategy)),\n        rate_limiting_enabled_(rate_limit_settings.enabled_) {\n    retry_timer_ = dispatcher.createTimer([this]() -> void { establishNewStream(); });\n    if (rate_limiting_enabled_) {\n      // Default Bucket contains 100 tokens maximum and refills at 10 tokens/sec.\n      limit_request_ = std::make_unique<TokenBucketImpl>(\n          rate_limit_settings.max_tokens_, time_source_, rate_limit_settings.fill_rate_);\n      drain_request_timer_ = dispatcher.createTimer([this]() {\n        if (stream_ != nullptr) {\n          callbacks_->onWriteable();\n        }\n      });\n    }\n  }\n\n  void establishNewStream() override {\n    stream_intentionally_closed_ = false;\n    ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Establishing new gRPC bidi stream to {} for {}\", async_client_.destination(),\n              service_method_.DebugString());\n    if (stream_ != nullptr) {\n      ENVOY_LOG(warn, \"gRPC bidi stream to {} for {} already exists!\", async_client_.destination(),\n                service_method_.DebugString());\n      return;\n    }\n    stream_ = async_client_->start(service_method_, *this, Http::AsyncClient::StreamOptions());\n    if (stream_ == nullptr) {\n      ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Unable to establish new stream to configuration server {}\",\n                async_client_.destination());\n      callbacks_->onEstablishmentFailure();\n      setRetryTimer();\n      return;\n    }\n    control_plane_stats_.connected_state_.set(1);\n    callbacks_->onStreamEstablished();\n  }\n\n  bool grpcStreamAvailable() const override { return stream_ != nullptr; (The push() doesn't matter\n    // because we always attempt this drain immediately after the push). Basically, a change in\n    // queue length is not \"meaningful\" until it has persisted until here. We need the\n    // if(>0 || used) to keep this stat from being wrongly marked interesting by a pointless set(0)\n    // and needlessly taking up space. Subscription Factory\\n**source/common/config/subscription_factory_impl.h/cc**:\\n- `SubscriptionFactoryImpl::subscriptionFromConfigSource()` creates subscriptions\\n- Calls `Utility::checkTransportVersion()` to validate v2 is not used\\n- Delegates to appropriate subscription type (GRPC, DELTA_GRPC, REST, etc.)\\n\\n## Migration Strategy\\n\\nEnvoy v1.31.2 implements v2-to-v3 API migration through:\\n\\n1. **Protocol Buffer Versioning**: Proto files use UDPA versioning annotations (`udpa.annotations.versioning.previous_message_type`) to document v2-v3 mapping\\n\\n2. **Field Renames**: The v2-v3 transition involved field name changes (e.g., Node type reference, error handling structure) documented in proto annotations\\n\\n3. **Template-Based Dual Support**: The xds_mux implementation uses C++ templates to support both SOTW (with DiscoveryRequest/Response) and Delta (with DeltaDiscoveryRequest/Response) xDS modes, all using v3 types\\n\\n4. **Legacy vs New Implementation**: Two parallel implementations exist:\\n   - `grpc_mux_impl`: Direct v3 implementation for backward compatibility\\n   - `xds_mux/grpc_mux_impl`: Templated flexible implementation supporting both subscription modes\\n\\n5. **Version Enforcement**: The configuration layer explicitly rejects v2 transport API versions, forcing migration to v3\\n\\n## Important Note\\n\\nIn Envoy v1.31.2, **v2 support has been completely removed from the source code**. The v2 proto definitions still exist in the repository (api/envoy/api/v2/ and api/envoy/service/discovery/v2/) for reference and documentation purposes, but the C++ implementation uses only v3 types. The dual-version subscription handling is achieved through:\\n- Template specialization for Delta vs SOTW modes (both v3)\\n- Proto versioning annotations indicating v2-v3 mapping\\n- Configuration validation preventing v2 usage\\n\\nThe actual v2-to-v3 conversion would have occurred at proto-generation time during the API migration phase, not at runtime in this version of Envoy.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":950,"cache_read_input_tokens":84481,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":950},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"8d1496db-954b-4403-9ba2-b3e1ab4ad5d0","uuid":"3dd0e3f0-f4f0-41ed-92bb-2c282ea0b285"}

Subscription State Handlers\\n**Delta Subscription State:**\\n- `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/delta_subscription_state.h/cc`: Legacy implementation handling `envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryResponse`\\n- `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/delta_subscription_state.h/cc`: Newer implementation as `BaseSubscriptionState<DeltaDiscoveryResponse, DeltaDiscoveryRequest>`\\n- Method `handleResponse(const envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryResponse& message)` processes delta responses\\n\\n**State-of-the-World Subscription State:**\\n- `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/sotw_subscription_state.h/cc`: Implements SOTW protocol with `envoy::service::discovery::v3::DiscoveryRequest` and `DiscoveryResponse`\\n- Method `handleGoodResponse(const envoy::service::discovery::v3::DiscoveryResponse& message)` processes SOTW responses\\n\\n### 5. Base Subscription State Template\\n**source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/subscription_state.h**:\\n- `BaseSubscriptionState<RS, RQ>` template provides common protocol state handling for both delta and SOTW variants\\n- `handleResponse(const RS& response)` method handles version management and ACKing\\n- All instantiations use v3 proto types (DiscoveryRequest, DiscoveryResponse, DeltaDiscoveryRequest, DeltaDiscoveryResponse)\\n\\n### 6. gRPC Stream and Failover\\n**source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_stream.h** and **grpc_mux_failover.h**:\\n- `GrpcStream<RequestProto, ResponseProto>` template handles actual gRPC communication\\n- Instantiated with v3 discovery types for both primary and failover streams\\n- `sendMessage(const RequestProto& request)` sends v3 requests\\n- `onReceiveMessage(ResponseProtoPtr<ResponseProto>&& message)` receives v3 responses\\n\\n### 7. Version Checking and Validation\\n**source/common/config/utility.h/cc**:\\n- `Utility::checkTransportVersion()` validates API version configuration\\n- Currently rejects v2 transport API version with message: \\\"The v2 xDS major version has been removed and is no longer supported\\\"\\n- Only allows `ApiVersion::AUTO` or `ApiVersion::V3`\\n\\n**source/common/config/api_version.h**:\\n- Defines `API_NO_BOOST()` macro for forcing specific proto versions (comment mentions preventing API boosting)\\n\\n### 8. Subscription Factory\\n**source/common/config/subscription_factory_impl.h/cc**:\\n- `SubscriptionFactoryImpl::subscriptionFromConfigSource()` creates subscriptions\\n- Calls `Utility::checkTransportVersion()` to validate v2 is not used\\n- Delegates to appropriate subscription type (GRPC, DELTA_GRPC, REST, etc.)\\n\\n## Migration Strategy\\n\\nEnvoy v1.31.2 implements v2-to-v3 API migration through:\\n\\n1. **Protocol Buffer Versioning**: Proto files use UDPA versioning annotations (`udpa.annotations.versioning.previous_message_type`) to document v2-v3 mapping\\n\\n2. **Field Renames**: The v2-v3 transition involved field name changes (e.g., Node type reference, error handling structure) documented in proto annotations\\n\\n3. **Template-Based Dual Support**: The xds_mux implementation uses C++ templates to support both SOTW (with DiscoveryRequest/Response) and Delta (with DeltaDiscoveryRequest/Response) xDS modes, all using v3 types\\n\\n4. **Legacy vs New Implementation**: Two parallel implementations exist:\\n   - `grpc_mux_impl`: Direct v3 implementation for backward compatibility\\n   - `xds_mux/grpc_mux_impl`: Templated flexible implementation supporting both subscription modes\\n\\n5. **Version Enforcement**: The configuration layer explicitly rejects v2 transport API versions, forcing migration to v3\\n\\n## Important Note\\n\\nIn Envoy v1.31.2, **v2 support has been completely removed from the source code**. The v2 proto definitions still exist in the repository (api/envoy/api/v2/ and api/envoy/service/discovery/v2/) for reference and documentation purposes, but the C++ implementation uses only v3 types. The dual-version subscription handling is achieved through:\\n- Template specialization for Delta vs SOTW modes (both v3)\\n- Proto versioning annotations indicating v2-v3 mapping\\n- Configuration validation preventing v2 usage\\n\\nThe actual v2-to-v3 conversion would have occurred at proto-generation time during the API migration phase, not at runtime in this version of Envoy.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
